# C Sharp Algorithms

> Algorithms are one of the fundamental pillars in every software application, and once you understand them, you can create more efficient and maintainable programs. In this course, instructor Kathryn Hodge uses instruction and hands-on practice to show you how to create better C# programs by using efficient algorithms. Kathryn discusses what makes an algorithm effective, as well as how to make info

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms) | Advanced | 32K learners

### Introduction

#### Improve your C# applications with efficient algorithms
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Kathryn] Algorithms are one of the fundamental pillars in every software application.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=5)** In order to create more advanced and sophisticated applications, it's important to hone in on the algorithms your software is using.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=14)** Some are more efficient than others in terms of time and space complexity.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=18)** And it's essential to understand the speed implications of the software you're creating.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=24)** It's also important to understand the assumptions you're making about the data you're working with.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=30)** Otherwise, your algorithm might not work as expected.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=34)** Hi, I'm Kathryn Hodge and I'm a software engineer.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=37)** In this course, we'll look at how to create more efficient programs by exploring different types of algorithms.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=44)** Many of these algorithms are built right into the C# language and they can be a great choice.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=50)** However, most of the time you'll need to create a custom algorithm in order to work with your data in exactly the way you want.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=58)** In this course, we'll explore what makes a given algorithm effective as well as how to make informed assumptions about your data in order to speed up that processing time.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=69)** We'll also discover how to leverage different data structures in order to make your algorithms more efficient.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/improve-your-c-sharp-applications-with-efficient-algorithms?u=76281980&t=75)** Without any further delay, let's get started.

#### What is an algorithm?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] An algorithm is a series of defined instructions that perform some task.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=5)** For example, we can break apart the task of making a sandwich into an algorithm.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=11)** The first instruction would be to retrieve the ingredients as well as any tools, such as a knife.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=17)** Then you might slice the bread and spread mustard or mayo on the sandwich.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=23)** Next, you would place ham and cheese on the sandwich.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=26)** Then combine the pieces of bread together, making your sandwich complete.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=33)** Most of us have made many sandwiches in our lifetime so we don't think about each individual step that needs to occur in order to perform the task of making a sandwich.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=43)** However, a computer is different.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=46)** Every step must be laid out in order to complete a software-based task.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=52)** Given this, in C#, almost everything you create is a part of some algorithm.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=58)** Every line of code you write is an instruction that is a step in achieving some task.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=64)** It might be to find the even numbers in an array or to validate whether a string has certain properties.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=73)** There are also many different sets of instructions that complete the same task.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=78)** Some sets are more efficient than others, but they all have defined instructions that set out to complete a task.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=86)** That's what makes an algorithm an algorithm.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>

> **Analogies:** for example (1), such as (1)
> **CLI Commands:** find (1)
> **Code Keywords:** this, (1)

#### How to optimize an algorithm
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] There are many different ways to complete a given task.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=3)** As such, there are many different algorithms to solve a problem.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=8)** Some algorithms are more efficient and others are less efficient.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=12)** For example, with our sandwich algorithm, one way to make a sandwich is to go to the store for each ingredient.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=20)** You make multiple trips to the store and you start making the sandwich after gathering all the ingredients.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=28)** Before, we assumed we had all the proper ingredients and required tools in the kitchen.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=35)** By making this assumption, we were able to save time by not running to the store.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=40)** The same is true for algorithms.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=43)** To make an algorithm more efficient, you have to make an assumption about your data.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=48)** You might assume your data is sorted or that it will only contain integers or strings.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=54)** Maybe it will only contain positive integers or strings with only alphabetical characters.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=60)** With these assumptions, we can skip steps, normalizing the string or for the sandwich analogy, running to the grocery store.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=69)** This makes our algorithms more efficient.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=72)** However, it's very important to understand what assumptions your algorithm is making.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=78)** If you make a wrong assumption about your data, the algorithm will likely not perform the task as expected.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=86)** A slow working algorithm is always preferred to a fast algorithm that isn't trustworthy and can spit out a wrong response.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-optimize-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=94)** That's why it's essential to make informed assumptions about your data, and you can leverage these assumptions to optimize your algorithms.

#### Optimize an algorithm in C#
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] While studying algorithmic theory is important, it's vital to apply the theory to practice.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=7)** Let's modify a C# algorithm and make it more efficient.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=11)** In this sample code, we have an algorithm called findMaximum.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=15)** This finds the largest of three numbers.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=19)** If there are duplicate entries, we still return whatever the maximum is.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=24)** You can find it in the exercise files of this course.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=28)** Now inside the algorithm, we do several comparisons in order to find that maximum.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=34)** We can actually eliminate some of these comparisons and make our algorithm more efficient using assumptions.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=41)** On the first line of the algorithm, we check if A is greater than B.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=46)** Then later on, we check the opposite, is B greater than A.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=51)** Instead of doing multiple checks with each input, what if we kept track of the maximum using a variable?
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=59)** Let's create a new function with our refactor.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=63)** Static int, we'll call it findMaximum2 and it will take in those three numbers.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=73)** The value of the max will start off at A.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=76)** Then we'll compare B to the max.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=80)** If B is greater than the max, then we'll set the max to B.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=84)** In the previous implementation, we had to add checks for if A and B or A and C were equal.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=91)** With this implementation, it doesn't matter because the value is already stored in the max variable.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=98)** At this point in the execution, the max variable contains whatever the maximum of A and B is.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=105)** To check whether C is greater, we just need to add one more comparison.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=110)** If C is greater than the max, then we'll set the max to C.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=116)** Now the maximum variable contains the maximum of A, B, and C, and we can return it from the function.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=126)** Let's test our new algorithm's implementation.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=133)** To run the code, we have a few different options.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=137)** We can run it in the terminal with dotnet run.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=141)** In the output, we get the maximum for each function call.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=146)** Another option is to set up a run configuration with your IDE.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=151)** I'm using VS Code and this is the configuration that will run your application as a console application with the output to the integrated terminal.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=161)** Using a run configuration allows you to add break points to your code.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=167)** Let's put a break point on line 25.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=171)** To run it, we'll use the play button.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=176)** The program's execution stops on line 25.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=180)** We can see the values for each of our variables at this point in the execution.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=186)** Then we can walk through the algorithm using the step over function.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=193)** The max is reset to B and the max is set to C.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=200)** Then we return it.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=206)** In the terminal, we see three.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=210)** We'll stop it for now.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=213)** No matter how you run your code, you'll get the maximum for each set of values in the output.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=220)** With the new implementation, we did only two comparisons per call.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=225)** The code is also more readable with the defined variable and less comparisons.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=231)** With this algorithm, we use the assumption that the max variable will contain the maximum for that point in the program's execution.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=239)** When we check the max with C, we assume that the max variable holds the maximum of A and B.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/optimize-an-algorithm-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=246)** This allows us to do less comparisons and optimize the algorithm.

#### How to describe the time complexity of an algorithm
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Some algorithms are more efficient than others and we often describe an algorithm sufficiency using Big-O notation.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=8)** Big-O notation allows us to compare algorithms independent of input size.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=15)** For example, let's say, we wanted to compare search algorithms.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=20)** If the item we're searching for will always be the first or the last element of the list, we can say it takes constant time or O of one time.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=31)** No matter what the input size is, we just have to check the first and last element to find our answer.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=39)** If the item we're searching for is somewhere in the list but we don't know where, we might have to check every single element.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=47)** In the best case, the item we're looking for would be the first item we check.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=52)** In the worst case, the element would not exist in the list and we'd have to check every single item.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=59)** Most algorithms have a best case and worst case performance time and they're often not the same.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=66)** For this search algorithm, the best case would be constant time.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=71)** The first item we check is the item we're searching for.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=74)** The worst case would be linear time.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=77)** As the input size increases, the search time increases.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=81)** With Big-O notation, the worst case would be O of N where N is the input size.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=89)** In deciding which algorithm to use, we often use the worst case time complexity as a deciding factor.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=96)** However, if the worst case happens only 5% of the time, then it might be useful to consider the best case as well.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=106)** The more informed assumptions we're able to make about our data, the more efficient we can make our algorithms.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=113)** With the first search algorithm, we assume that the item we're searching for will be the first or last element.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=120)** This cuts the best case and the worst case down to constant time.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=125)** With the other algorithm, we do not make this assumption which lengthens the algorithms worst time to O event.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=133)** Some other common time complexities and algorithm can have are logarithmic or O of log n, an exponential, or O of N squared.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=144)** Constant time is the most efficient out of all of these with N squared being the least efficient.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=150)** With N as a generic input size, we're able to compare these notations in terms of efficiency.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=157)** We also use this notation to describe space complexity.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=162)** Does the algorithm use constant space or as much space as the size of the input?
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=168)** This can be another factor in deciding which algorithm to use to complete a task.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/how-to-describe-the-time-complexity-of-an-algorithm?u=76281980&t=174)** However, no matter how efficient your algorithms are, Big-O notation allows you to compare them, regardless of input size.

> **Code Keywords:** case, (2), let (1), for. (1)

#### Normalize strings in C#
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Before processing a string, it can be helpful to normalize it to a common form in order to make your algorithm more efficient.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=9)** Let's say you're searching for a particular letter within a string.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=14)** You could search for that letter once in the lowercase form and once in the uppercase form.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=21)** This means you would have to run two different searches to find out if the letter exists.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=27)** Now, another way to go about this is to convert the string to all lowercase.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=33)** With this approach, you could search for the letter in the lowercase form and only have to search for one form of the letter.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=41)** With two different forms, you're still iterating through the string twice.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=46)** But if the number of different forms the letter can appear as increases, the amount you have to search stays the same.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=54)** It also makes your code less complex by searching for one form or one type of the data.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=62)** This is one way to normalize your string data, converting all the characters to a certain case, either uppercase or lowercase or some other form.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=73)** Instead of normalizing your input, another option is to limit your input to only a certain type.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=80)** For example, your processing algorithm would only take in strings with all lowercase letters and it could use a validation algorithm to deny any other type of input.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=93)** However, we want our algorithms to be flexible so we can reuse them for strings with many different contents.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=101)** Normalizing your input to a common form can help you accomplish this.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=107)** Let's look at how we can normalize data in C#.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=112)** To start, we'll create a function called NormalizeString.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=122)** Previously, we validated the contents of the string.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=126)** Here, we'll actually be creating a new string, a normalized string.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=132)** It will have all the characters of the old string, but in the lowercase form.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=137)** To do this, we'll access the string input and use the ToLower method.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=144)** Now this will return a new string, so we need to save it out to a variable.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=150)** We'll call it lowercased.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=153)** Now ToLower follows a pattern that's actually pretty common for many algorithms.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=159)** Instead of modifying the input data, a new piece of data is returned based on the input.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=166)** We also get some other operations to make our data uniform with the C# standard library.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=173)** If we take our lowercase string, we can use the Trim method.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=178)** This will remove the white spaces from each end of the input data.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=184)** Again, this will return a new string, so we'll save it as trimmed.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=190)** Now for our processing algorithm, let's say there are certain characters we don't want to use or don't want to consider.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=198)** We want to remove them from the string.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=201)** We can do this using the Replace function.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=205)** We can replace the character we don't care about with the empty string.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=211)** In order to replace something with the empty string, both inputs will need to be strings, and so we've wrapped this comma character in a string.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=222)** Let's combine this into a single line.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=227)** We'll use the input.ToLower, then we'll trim the output of that, then we'll replace that comma character with the empty string.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=241)** Step-by-step, we'll normalize the string.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=245)** Let's test it out.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=250)** We'll say Hello There, BUDDY.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=257)** With this input, the algorithm will convert the string to lowercase, trim off the spaces and then remove the comma.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=266)** Let's run it.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=269)** The output is normalized.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=271)** It's all lowercase with no commas and there are no extra spaces on the ends.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/normalize-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=278)** When we normalize our data to a common form, we make our algorithms more flexible, more efficient, and easier to read and maintain.

#### Create algorithm-driven strings in C#
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Another standard programming task is to create a new string based on input data.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=6)** We've seen this a bit previously with toLower and replace where a string is inputted into a function, and a new string is created using the data from the input string.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=19)** These two functions are built into the standard library, but let's try creating our own functions that dynamically build a string using input data.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=30)** The algorithm we'll create will build the reverse of whatever string is inputted.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=36)** It will reverse the string.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=42)** We'll want to cover our base cases where the string is null or empty.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=48)** We can use the built-in string function to do that.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=51)** If either of these cases are true, we'll just return the input.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=59)** That covers our base cases.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=61)** When starting your software development journey, sometimes it can feel like you're cheating by using the functions built into the language or the standard library.

>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=83)** If that happens to be using a standard library function, great.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=88)** If it happens to be something custom that you have to build, that's also great.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=94)** Typically if there's something already built to do the job and it does the job well, it's better to use that than create your own algorithm from scratch that does the exact same thing.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=108)** The function that's already built is likely well tested and used by many other systems and programs.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=115)** So if it does what you need, use it.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=117)** Now let's reverse the string.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=120)** When performing operations on strings, it can be very easy to create a bunch of unnecessary strings as you're trying to build your output.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=130)** This happens because strings are immutable.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=133)** You can't change them once they're created.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=136)** To make our algorithm more efficient so that it doesn't create this unnecessary extra data, we'll use a string builder.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=148)** The string builder is from the system.text library.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=152)** So we'll need to add an import at the top.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=160)** Now string builder works differently than a string in memory.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=165)** When the string builder is modified, it doesn't create a new string builder.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=170)** Instead, it dynamically expands memory to accommodate the modified string.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=176)** This is what makes it more efficient than a regular string.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=181)** To reverse the string, we'll use a for loop.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=186)** However, instead of iterating through the string starting at the first index, we'll start at the last index.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=195)** That's input.Length - 1.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=199)** On each iteration, we'll decrement I by one.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=203)** And we'll continue to decrement until we get to the end of the string at index zero.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=209)** Using a for loop in this way, allows us to iterate through the string backwards, which can be good for many algorithms, including this one.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=219)** Since we are going through the string backwards, all we have to do is append the character we're at to the string builder.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=230)** We'll access the character in the string at index I and append it to reversed.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=239)** At the end of the loops execution, the reverse string will be built and we can return the new string.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=248)** Since reverse is a string builder, we can use ToString to convert it to a string.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=254)** And that's our algorithm.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=256)** Let's try it out.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=277)** Here we have a few test cases, including those base cases.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=282)** Let's run it.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=285)** In the output, we get nothing for the base cases, which is expected.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=290)** We also get the other inputs reversed.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=294)** The reverse algorithm uses each character exactly.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=298)** So the casing remains the same.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=301)** It also works regardless of what type of character is used, including punctuation.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=308)** Now reversing a string is a pretty common operation in programming, and there are several ways to do it in C#.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=316)** With this algorithm, we did it with a more bare bones approach where we iterated through each character and built the new string one character at a time.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=327)** Another way we can reverse a string is by converting our data into a data type that already has a built-in reverse method.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=338)** We'll look at arrays more in the next chapter, but array has a reverse function.
>
> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=344)** If we can convert the string into an array, we can use this function and put that array as input.
>
> **[5:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=352)** With the string, we get access to the ToChar array method.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=357)** This converts the string into a character array.
>
> **[6:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=362)** Let's pass the array into the reverse function.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=368)** This will modify the array so that the contents are reversed.
>
> **[6:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=372)** It does not create a new array.
>
> **[6:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=375)** This means we can convert the character array back into a string.
>
> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=381)** This new string will have the characters reversed.
>
> **[6:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=386)** Now we aren't done yet.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=388)** We need to make sure that the string is not null.
>
> **[6:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=392)** Otherwise, we'll get an error when we try to convert it to a character array.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=397)** Let's use the same base condition as before.
>
> **[6:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=404)** There's the function. Let's call it.
>
> **[6:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=410)** Instead of reverse, we'll use Reverse2 and we'll run it again.
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=419)** The output is the same.
>
> **[7:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=421)** Even with a common programming task, there's never just one way to write an algorithm.
>
> **[7:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-algorithm-driven-strings-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=427)** Each have their pros and cons, depending on the amount of complexity you want to introduce to the code base.

#### Solution: reverse each word
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=0)** Let's create an algorithm that reverses each word in a sentence.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=4)** First, we'll split up the sentence into words.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=8)** The constraints say that a word is separated by spaces.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=12)** This means we can use the split method on the sentence and pass in the space character as a delimiter.
>

>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=26)** To reverse each word, we can use our reverse helper method.

> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=31)** We'll use link to select each word.

> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=35)** And then reverse it with our helper method.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=39)** Then we'll turn this into an array so we can have an array of reversed words.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=48)** Now all we have to do is join the words back together into a sentence.
>

>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=61)** Here we separate each reversed word with the space to create the reversedSentence string.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=69)** We now have a string with each word reversed.

> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=81)** Let's run the program.

> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=84)** In the output, we get, "Sally is a great worker", but each word within the string is reversed.

> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=91)** The casing also remains the same.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=94)** Let's try another example.

> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=98)** We'll do racecar madam.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-reverse-each-word-19866902?u=76281980&t=105)** The program says were correct, but racecar and madden looked the same.

### 2. Array Algorithms

#### Linear search arrays in C#
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] As a software engineer, you'll need to search through data structures, using algorithms in order to retrieve relevant data.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=8)** With a search algorithm, you often input the data you need to search and the item you're trying to find.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=16)** Sometimes the algorithm will return true or false depending on whether the item exists or it will return the item itself with more data, let's take a look at how we can search for data in the array data structure.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=33)** One option is to do a linear search, also called a sequential search, where we look at each item in the array.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=40)** One at a time, in order, we'll do this using a for each loop.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=55)** For each integer in the array, we check if it matches the thing we're looking for, N.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=61)** If so, we return true.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=64)** If we search through the entire array and still cannot find N then it must not exist in the array and we can return false.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=73)** Another option is to return the data itself, instead of a Boolean.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=78)** If we find the data we'll return N, if we don't find the data, we can return a Sentinel value.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=89)** This is a value that will never be the value of N and it can serve as a not found value.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=97)** Both of these will be ENTs.

> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=99)** So we'll need to change the return type to ENT.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=103)** Instead of returning a Sentinel value, we could also return null, but we need to add a question mark to the return type.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=111)** This lets null be a proper value to return from the function.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=116)** Let's try running it.

>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=282)** For each item, we'll print it to the console.

> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=313)** There are some alternatives to find and find all that work with array indices.

> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/linear-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=319)** However, I find these two functions to be most useful when searching for data within arrays.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** function (6), let (5), case, (2), pass (2), for, (1)
> **CLI Commands:** find (16)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1), is called (1)
> **Env Vars:** ent (1)

#### Binary search arrays in C#
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Searching data is a common task in software development.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=4)** In order to optimize our search algorithm, we'll need to make assumptions about the data.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=10)** For example, if you know the array will be sorted, you can start at the middle and then work your way towards the beginning or the end of the array, depending on where the items should be located.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=24)** If this happens to be the case, one algorithm we can use is binary search.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=30)** Binary search is a divide and conquer algorithm where in each step it halves the number of elements it has to search through.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=39)** For example, if we had an array of sorted numbers, the algorithm would start at the middle.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=46)** Then depending on whether the item we're searching for is greater than or less than the item we're looking at, it would continue its search in that portion of the array.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=58)** Let's say we were looking for the number 45.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=62)** The algorithm would start its search at index three, or item 19.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=68)** Since 19 is less than 45, it would continue its search in the second half of the array with 23, 45 and 79.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=80)** The mid point of this array is 45.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=83)** And that happens to be the element we're looking for.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=86)** This means, instead of doing six comparisons, we only had to do two to find the element.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=94)** If we had to look at each element, the algorithm would run an O(n) time or linear time.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=101)** However, since we have the number of elements with each comparison, this algorithm runs and (log(n)) time.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=110)** We were only able to do this because we assumed the array was sorted.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=115)** If it was not sorted, then this algorithm would not work as expected.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=121)** Let's try implementing binary search in C Sharp.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=125)** This algorithm will input an array and the item we're searching for.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=131)** There are lots of different things that this function could return.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=135)** Whether that's if the item exists, a bullion or even the index where the element was found.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=143)** To keep things simple, we'll return a bullion, true or false, depending on whether the item exists.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=150)** Now for the implementation.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=153)** The first step is to create variables for the min and max indices.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=158)** This will help us bucket the inner array we're searching through.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=163)** To start, that's the full array.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=165)** So the min will start at zero and the max will start at the end of the array.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=171)** Or inputArray.Length - 1.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=175)** We'll want to continue to search through the array until the min is greater than or equal to the max.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=183)** This makes the inner array length zero.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=187)** If we get to that case, then the item must not be in the array.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=192)** Let's create a while loop.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=194)** And while the min is less than or equal to the max, we'll continue to search for the item.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=201)** If we don't find the item in the loop, we'll return false, because again, it must not exist in the array.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=209)** In the while loop, we'll create a midpoint using the min and max to start our search.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=216)** The midpoint can be calculated with the min plus the max divided by two.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=223)** Then we'll check whether this item is equal to the item we're searching for.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=231)** If they match, we'll return true.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=233)** We found the item in the array.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=236)** Otherwise we need to search through the sub array of this array.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=242)** We'll need to determine whether to search through the front half or the back half of the inner array.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=249)** We can do this by checking whether the item is greater than or less than the item at the midpoint.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=257)** If the item is less than the item at the mid point, then we need to search through the front half of the array.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=265)** We can do that by setting the max equal to the mid minus one.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=271)** We're closing in that inner array.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=276)** If the first two conditions are false, then the item must be greater than the item at the midpoint.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=283)** We need to search through the back half of the array.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=288)** We can do that by setting the min equal to the midpoint plus one.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=294)** This makes that inner array smaller, and that's it.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=298)** Let's try it out.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=305)** BinarySearch and we'll input the array with the item five.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=314)** And it works as expected.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=316)** It's important to note that we are making some serious assumptions here.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=322)** We're assuming that the array is sorted.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=325)** And we're also assuming that the array is sorted in ascending order.
>
> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=330)** If these were not true for the input array, our implementation would not work as expected.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=337)** Instead, we'd have to normalize our array by sorting it in ascending order.
>
> **[5:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=343)** This would add to the time complexity of the algorithm.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=347)** If we had to sort it, how long would it take?
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=351)** Depending on which sorting algorithm you're using, it could take longer to sort the array than just to do a linear search.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=359)** At that point, it depends on how useful it is to have your data sorted.
>
> **[6:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=365)** Will you be running multiple searches on the data making it optimal to do the sorting, or do you just need to do one search?
>
> **[6:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=375)** In that case, a linear search would be more useful.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=378)** Either way, it's important to consider your assumptions and how you're using your data in the context of your code base.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=387)** Now C Sharp does have a built-in function for binary search.
>
> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=393)** You pass in the array and the item you're looking for.
>
> **[6:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=398)** While this can be useful, it's important to know how it works before applying it to your data.
>
> **[6:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/binary-search-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=404)** That's why we spent the time here exploring the binary search algorithm.

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Aggregating and filtering data, are standard programming operations.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=5)** When aggregating data, you combine two or more datasets into a single dataset.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=11)** Sometimes, when combining these datasets, you'll want to filter out data that does not meet your requirements.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=19)** Imagine we have two arrays and we want to create a new array that contains all the even numbers from each array.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=27)** There are a few different ways we could accomplish this.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=31)** One way is to merge the arrays and then remove the invalid items.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=37)** Another is to check each item to see if it meets the requirements before adding it to the combined array.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=45)** We can also sort each array.
>

> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=69)** To keep things simple, we're going to take the second approach where we check each item before adding it to the new array.

> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=84)** It will return a new array with only the even values.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=89)** To keep track of these even numbers, we'll create an array list called result.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=98)** We could create a new array instead, but we don't know how many even numbers will be in each array.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=105)** With the array list, we can add as many even numbers as we need to without worrying about an index out of bounds error.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=114)** Or creating an array with too much space.

> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=124)** We'll start with the for each loop because it doesn't matter where these even numbers are located.

> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/aggregate-and-filter-arrays-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=131)** To check if the number is even, we can use the modulo operator.

#### Reverse an array in C#
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] As a software engineer, requirements can change, and sometimes, you'll need to change the ordering of your data.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=8)** For example, you may need to swap elements or reverse your dataset entirely.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=14)** Let's look at how to reverse an array in C-sharp.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=18)** One way is to copy all the contents into a new array, but in reverse order.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=25)** To start, we'd create a new array to hold the reversed contents.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=32)** It would have the same length as the input array since no new contents are being added or removed, just rearranged.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=43)** Then, we'd iterate through the reversed array and add the contents from the input array in reverse order.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=51)** We'd start at index i, going up to the reverse.length, incrementing i each time while i is less than the length.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=62)** Then, we'll set the value at index i equal to input at input.length minus i minus one.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=73)** This will take whatever's at the back of the input array and put it to the front of the reversed array.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=79)** It will also take whatever's at the front of the input array and put it at the end of the reversed array.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=88)** Once the iteration is complete, we can return the reversed array, which will have the input contents in reverse order.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=97)** Let's run it.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=103)** And the output is as expected.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=105)** We get six all the way down to one.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=108)** The contents in reversed order.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=111)** Now since no new contents are being added or removed, we can actually do this algorithm in place, modifying the contents of the input array without creating a new reversed array.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=125)** We would swap the items around in place and put them in reverse order.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=131)** This reverse in place function will return void because we'll modify the input array instead of creating a new value.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=140)** With this algorithm, we'll be swapping elements, so we only need to iterate half as many times or the size of the array divided by two.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=151)** If we happen to get an array that has an odd number of elements, the middle element does not need to be moved.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=157)** It stays in the same place in the reversed array.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=162)** For each iteration, we'll want to swap the item at index i with the item at index input.length minus i minus one.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=175)** This will take the items at the back of the array and put them at the front of the array.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=181)** It will also take the items at the front of the array and put them at the back of the array.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=187)** We can bring the items from the back of the array to the front with input i equals input input.length minus i minus one.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=198)** However, we do run into a problem.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=201)** We overwrite the values at the front of the array.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=205)** We can fix this by saving the item at index i before we do the assignment.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=213)** We'll create a temp variable and save the item at index i.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=219)** With the temp variable, we can take this item at the smaller index and put it at the larger index.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=227)** We'll set the item at input.length minus i minus one equal to temp.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=234)** And that's it.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=235)** That's the algorithm.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=237)** Let's try it with our array.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=246)** We'll use the reverse in place algorithm and then print out that same arrays contents.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=258)** The array should be modified so the contents should be in reverse order.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=265)** The output is as expected.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=267)** Now what if we ran the algorithm again?
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=271)** The reverse of a reverse is the original content and we get the original ordering in the console.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/reverse-an-array-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=281)** Understanding how to work with data in place and move it around in memory using variables is essential to creating efficient algorithms.
