#### Leverage the HashSet type in C# algorithms
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The C# standard library provides a few data types for working with unique items, but you'll need to leverage these types in order to manipulate data in exactly the way you want.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=13)** For example, let's say we have two arrays and we want to find out what elements are present in the first array, but not the second, given both arrays are unsorted.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=25)** With this example, three, two, and five are present in both arrays, but only four and eight are present in the first array.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=34)** This question we're asking, what elements are present in one array, but not the other, is really a question of membership.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=43)** We're asking what elements are a member of the first array, but not a member of the second array.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=49)** The HashSet is a great tool when working with questions of membership and we'll use it in our algorithm to find the answer to this problem.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=59)** Let's create an algorithm that finds what elements are present in the first array, but not the second.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=68)** This will take in two inputs, the first array and the second array.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=74)** In the implementation, we'll create a list to store the missing elements in the second array.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=84)** In order to determine whether an element is missing, we'll need to know what items are in the second array.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=91)** Then we can cross-check them with the first array.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=94)** We'll do this using a HashSet.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=103)** Then we'll put all the items in the second array inside the HashMap.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=108)** We can do this by iterating through the array.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=112)** We use a for-each loop because we don't care about the location or the ordering of the elements.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=118)** We just want to add them into the HashSet.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=123)** With these items added to the HashSet, we can iterate through the first array.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=128)** On each iteration, we'll check whether or not each element from the first array exists in the second.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=135)** Again, this is a question of membership.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=138)** Location and ordering do not matter so we'll use a for-each loop.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=144)** To check whether the item exists, we'll use the HashSet.contains and check for that item in the first array.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=154)** If it does exist, then we're all good.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=156)** We don't need to add anything to the missing elements list and we'll make that list plural.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=163)** However, if the item does not exist in the second array items, we've found a missing element and we'll want to add it to that missing elements list.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=177)** We can do that using the add method.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=181)** Once we've done this for every item in the first array, we can return the list of missing elements.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=188)** We found all the items that are in the first array, but not the second.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=193)** They're missing from that second array.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=197)** Let's test it out.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=200)** We'll call it in the main function.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=237)** Let's run it.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=240)** For the first call, three and one are not included in the second array.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=246)** For the second call, four and eight are not included.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=250)** This output is as expected.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=252)** With the HashSet, we were able to retrieve and search our data in constant time because each item stored in the HashSet is unique.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/leverage-the-hashset-type-in-c-sharp-algorithms?u=76281980&t=263)** We leveraged this uniqueness to create an efficient algorithm that uses the principle of membership.

#### Use the Dictionary type in C# algorithms

#### Solution: detect a cyclic linkedlist
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=0)** Let's create an algorithm that detects if a linked list has a cycle.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=5)** In order to determine if there's a cycle, we need to use the next pointers of the linked list.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=12)** We need to check that a given next pointer is not pointing to a node we've already seen in the list.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=19)** This is a question of membership, which makes the HashSet a great tool for this algorithm.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=26)** In our code, we'll iterate through the linked list, and every time we see a new node, we'll check if it's in the HashSet.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=34)** If it's not, we'll add it to the set.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=37)** If it is in the HashSet, this means we've seen the node before and there is a cycle in the list.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=44)** If we're able to get through the entire list without seeing the same node twice, then there's not a cycle in the list.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=52)** Let's implement this idea in code.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=57)** To start, we'll create a new HashSet that will store the nodes we've already seen in the list.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=66)** Then we'll create a current reference that will keep track of where we are in the list.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=74)** While the current is not equal to null, there are still elements in the list we need to check.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=82)** We need to check that the current node is not a node we've previously seen in the list.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=88)** We'll check if nodes contains our current element.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=94)** If it does, we'll return true because there is a cycle in the list.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=99)** We've seen the node before.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=103)** If this is not a node we've seen before, we can keep track of it by adding it to our HashSet.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=112)** Then we'll increment the current node by pointing it to current.Next.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=122)** If we make it through the entire list without returning true, the list does not have a cycle and we can return false.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=131)** Let's try it out.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=134)** In the test code, we have a ListNode(1), a ListNode(2), and a ListNode(3).
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=140)** Then we set ListNode(3)'s next pointer to the head.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=146)** This creates a cycle in the list.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=149)** Let's run it.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=153)** And we get the correct answer.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=157)** Our code returns true.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=160)** This list does have a cycle.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=163)** Now let's talk about time complexity.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=166)** With the HashSet, we were able to check in constant time whether a given node was one we had seen before.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-detect-a-cyclic-linkedlist?u=76281980&t=173)** This means our algorithm runs in linear time and linear space, since we need to check every node if the list does not have a cycle.

### 6. Tree Algorithms

#### What is a tree?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] If you're working with nonlinear data in an algorithm, the tree data structure can be a useful tool.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=7)** A tree is a collection of nodes where each node might be linked to one, two, or even more nodes.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=15)** Now, the last time we talked about nodes, we talked about them in the context of a linked list, where each node was connected in a linear order, node by node.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=26)** The tree data structure presents a similar idea, but it applies to nonlinear data.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=33)** Just like a linked list, there is always a specific starting node in the tree data structure.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=39)** Instead of the head, we call it the root node.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=42)** The root node contains data as well as links to other nodes.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=48)** The linked nodes are called child nodes.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=51)** Since a given node in the tree can have many different nodes, this is where the data becomes non-linear.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=58)** Levels with multiple nodes start to form, and there are many different paths in the tree to take.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=65)** We also refer to the root node as the parent of these child nodes.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=70)** The root node itself has no parent.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=73)** The second level of nodes are both parent nodes and children nodes.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=78)** Their children to the root, but the parents of the nodes they're connected to.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=83)** For a tree to be a tree, it needs to have a collection of nodes that are connected in some way by links.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=91)** Some nodes might have zero children and others might have 15 children.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=97)** It's a very broad data structure, and we can apply constraints in order to access the data in an efficient manner.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=105)** We can actually think of a linked list as a very specialized type of tree structure.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=111)** It consists of a collection of nodes where each node has only one link and that link is a child node.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=118)** This is one example where we put a constraint on the exact structure of the tree.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=123)** Then we take those constraints to optimize certain operations.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=129)** Another example of this idea is a binary tree.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=133)** With a binary tree, each node can have a maximum of two direct child nodes.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=139)** This limits, how many elements can appear on each level of the tree.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=144)** At most, it would be two to the power of the number of levels in the tree.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=150)** This means if you're going down a path in the tree, it limits your decision to at most two options.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=157)** You can take the left path or the right path.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=161)** We can take this a step further with something called a binary search tree.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=167)** With the binary tree, we could have our elements in any order, as long as they were organized where each node had no more than two child nodes.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=177)** With the binary search tree, we add the constraint of order.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=182)** Items are stored in a particular order so they're easy to retrieve and find.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=187)** One constraint that the binary search tree adds, is that the value to the left child node must be less than its parent.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=196)** This means if you're searching for an element in the tree, you can check whether the element you're looking for is less than the node you're looking at.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=205)** If it is, you can continue your search down the left side of the tree confidently, knowing that it won't be on the right side of the tree.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=214)** The other side of this constraint, is that the right child node must have a greater value than its parent.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=222)** These constraints make the tree data structure more than just a collection of stuff strung together.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=228)** With the binary search tree, we have a data structure that naturally stays sorted without immense amounts of reshuffling.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=236)** This gives us a fairly efficient way to search for a given piece of data.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=242)** In fact, it cuts the best case search time down to log event.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=247)** Although the worst case is still linear since all the elements might be on one side of the tree.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-is-a-tree?u=76281980&t=253)** By adding constraints to basic data structure ideas, we can create tools that help make our algorithms more efficient.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **CLI Commands:** node (17), make (2), find (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (3)
> **Cross-References:** we talked about (2)
> **Code Keywords:** continue (1)
> **Analogies:** just like (1)

#### Create a binary search tree in C#
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - In C#, we can use nodes in a binary search tree manner to work with our non-linear data efficiently.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=8)** The fundamental concepts of a binary search tree are very similar to a linked list.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=15)** We'll use a node class, but instead of a next reference, we'll have references to the left and right notes.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=21)** Again, we can do this because we assume that a node will have at most two direct child nodes.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=28)** Let's try it.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=31)** We'll write class node and give it three attributes.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=37)** We'll give it a left node, a right node, and some data.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=45)** Then we'll also give each of these, get and set access, so they're easy to use in our algorithms.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=57)** Now this node class itself is a tree.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=60)** It contains left and right trees, as well as a piece of data.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=64)** It only becomes a binary search tree, when we use algorithms to constrain how we insert, remove and manipulate our data.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=73)** This means the binary search tree class will only contain algorithms for working with node data.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=81)** When we use these algorithms, we'll assume that the data is stored in a binary search tree way.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=88)** Similar to how we followed a given nodes next references with the linked list structure, we can follow the left and right node references to access and manipulate all the data and the tree.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=100)** We just need the root node.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=103)** Let's create an algorithm to add data to a node in a binary search tree manner.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=109)** It will return the node we inserted and take in a value that we want to insert in the tree.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=117)** It will also take in the root node, which is the node we want to insert the value into.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=124)** Now, if the root node is null, then the inputted value should be turned into the root node.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=131)** We can create a new node with roots equals new node root.data equals value.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=140)** Then we can return the root.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=143)** since it's the only element in the tree, no left or right reference changes are needed.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=148)** They're both still null.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=151)** Now, if the root is not null, then we need to insert the value on either the left side of the tree or the right side of the tree.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=160)** With the constraint of the binary search tree, if the value is less than the root, then we insert it on the left.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=173)** If the value is greater than the root, then we insert it on the right.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=180)** If the value is equal to the root, then we don't need to insert anything.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=185)** We'll just return the root, which is already implemented here.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=190)** We'll move this outside the if statement and return.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=196)** Now, in order to insert an item on the left side of the tree, we can leverage this algorithm we're working on right now.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=205)** We can set the root dot left equal to whatever is returned by the insert algorithm, when we insert the item on the left of the tree.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=215)** We'll reuse the function we're creating right now, but instead of inputting the root we'll input, the root dot left.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=226)** We can do this for the right side of the tree as well.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=231)** Here, we're calling a function within a function with different inputs.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=236)** This is called recursion.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=238)** We defined a core base case with the root null check, and by calling the same function with different inputs, we can find the right place in the tree where this value should be inserted.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=251)** When we find that place, we'll create the node and set it accordingly.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=256)** Since this function returns the node, we immediately set it to the left or right, and return it up the tree.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=265)** For example, let's say we had a node four with no left and right references.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=272)** If we wanted to insert the value two, we would insert it on the left side of the tree, since two is less than four.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=280)** The insert function would be called again, but now the value for the root would be null.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=287)** This means that a node with the value two would be created and returned from the insert call.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=294)** Then the execution would go back to the initial call setting two as the left node for the root four.
>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=303)** Now, there are other ways to implement this algorithm, but this option leverages recursion to encourage code reusability.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=311)** Another option would be to use recursion with the four loop or a while loop as tools within this algorithm.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=318)** Recursion is just another tool in your algorithm toolkit.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=323)** Let's test out this function.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=325)** We'll create a root node and insert data using the static binary search tree function.
>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=348)** Let's run it.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=351)** Now, we won't see anything in the output just yet because we're only inserting data not displaying it.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/create-a-binary-search-tree-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=359)** However it is stored in memory efficiently, and we can continue to develop more algorithms to better visualize and manipulate our data.

#### What are tree traversals?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] With the binary search tree, data is not stored with any ordering constraints.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=6)** Data is simply stored and retrieved, and each node is placed in the next available slot.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=13)** This means in order to search for an element or manipulate data in the tree, one must iterate through the tree.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=20)** We call this traversing a tree or visiting each node to display or manipulate its data.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=27)** When traversing a tree, we have a few different options, depending on which nodes we visit first and which nodes we visit last.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=36)** For example, one way we could traverse the tree, is to recursively traverse the left subtree, visit the root node, and then recursively traverse the rights of tree.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=48)** The left most subtree is nine with no children nodes, so that would be displayed first, then it's root is seven.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=57)** That has a right subtree of 10, so that would be next.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=61)** Continuing up the tree, the root is six and its right subtree has eight.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=67)** These nodes are visited in order from left to right, nine, seven, 10, six, eight, so we call this an inorder traversal.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=78)** Another option is to do a pre-order traversal.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=81)** In a pre-order traversal, the root is visited first, then the left and right subtrees are recursively traversed.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=90)** This means route six would be visited first, then we would recursively go down the left most subtree, visiting each node along the way.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=101)** This means seven would be visited next and then nine.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=105)** Once all the left nodes have been visited, then we would begin to visit the right nodes working our way back up the tree.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=113)** 10 is the right note of seven, so that would be visited next.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=117)** Then eight is the right note of six and that would be visited last.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=122)** With this traversal, six, seven, nine, 10, eight, the root is visited first, then its subtrees are visited recursively.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=132)** The last type of traversal we'll look at is the post order traversal where the root is visited last.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=139)** First, the left subtrees visited, then the right subtree and finally the root.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=146)** Thinking about this algorithm with our own tree, this means that the left most node would be visited first, nine.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=154)** Then the next right node would be visited 10.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=157)** The root of this subtree is seven, so that would be next followed by eight, which is to the right of six.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=165)** Then it would be finished up with six, the root of the tree.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=169)** With this path, nine, 10, seven, eight, six, the root is visited last after each subtree has been recursively traversed.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=179)** Now these are three common options for traversing the data in a binary tree.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=185)** Again, these work because we're making the assumption that each node will have at most two child nodes, which traversal algorithm you choose depends on your use case.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=198)** If you know you'll need to explore the roots of the trees before inspecting the leaves, the pre-order algorithm is a good option because he visit the roots before the leaves.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=209)** If the opposite is true, meaning you want to explore the leaves before the roots, the post order algorithm might be better suited.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=218)** If your tree is a binary search tree or has a sequence with its nodes, then the in order traversal might be best.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=226)** It will visit the nodes in order and flatten the tree back to its original order.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=232)** Each type of traversal can be a useful tool when working with trees, they each have their pros and cons.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/what-are-tree-traversals?u=76281980&t=239)** It just depends on how you want to manipulate your data.

#### Using recursion to implement tree traversals in C#
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] And a tree traversal algorithm each node in a tree is accessed in a particular order.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=6)** With the pre-order traversal, we visit the root first.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=10)** With the in order traversal, we recursively visit the left tree and then the root.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=16)** With the post order traversal, we visit the root last.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=20)** With each traversal, we apply the same pattern to parts of the tree.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=25)** Then we continue that pattern throughout the tree.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=29)** The concept of recursion can be a useful tool in this type of algorithm, because we're doing the same operation with a slight modification to the input.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=39)** Let's look at how we can apply this to tree traversal algorithms.

>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=129)** We visit the root and then recursively visit all the nodes in the left tree and the right tree.

> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=136)** Let's try it out using the debugger.

> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=148)** In order to access it we'll need to make sure this is public.

>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=167)** To run it using the debugger, we have this configuration.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=193)** On the first call the root is four.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=196)** The left and right nodes are one and three.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=200)** If we look in the terminal, four has been displayed.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=205)** The left node is about to be traversed.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=209)** If we click continue, this pre-order function will be called again.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=213)** But now with the root one.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=217)** Since the root is one, we display it in the console.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=221)** Then it will recursively display the eight and nine nodes.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=225)** These don't have any children, so we'll hit that base case.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=231)** We see eight and we'll see nine.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=236)** Once the left subtree has been recursively traversed, the right subtree must be traversed.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=242)** This makes the route three pressing continue again.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=246)** We see that on the side.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=249)** Six is on the left, so then that will be displayed.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=254)** Then there are no more nodes, so the function will end its execution.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=261)** In the console, we see the full pre-order output.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=265)** The root is displayed first and then the left and right subtree contents are displayed.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=272)** The in order and post ordered traversals will follow a similar pattern.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=276)** All we have to do is change where the root is displayed.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=281)** Let's copy and paste the implementation and change out the names.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=288)** For the in order traversal, the root is printed out after recursing the left subtree.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=294)** This means we'll move the console dot write statement to in-between the in order traversals.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=302)** We'll traverse the left subtree, display the root and then traverse the right sub tree.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=310)** We can do a similar thing for the post order traversal.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=315)** We'll copy this, change the names
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=329)** and move the printout to the last statement.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=334)** We traverse the left, the right, and then display the root.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=339)** Let's test this out.
>
> **[6:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=364)** We'll run it with .netrun.
>
> **[6:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=370)** With the in order traversal, we get the items back in sequential order.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=376)** With the post order traversal, we get the leaves and then the root for each sub tree.
>
> **[6:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=382)** With the tree structure, we have flexibility on how we iterate through our data.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/using-recursion-to-implement-tree-traversals-in-c-sharp?u=76281980&t=387)** This gives us more options so we can work with our data in the most efficient manner possible.

#### Solution: find height of binary tree
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=0)** Let's calculate the height of a tree.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=3)** We'll start off with the base case where the root of the tree is null.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=10)** If the root is null, then the height of the tree is zero because there are no nodes in the tree.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=18)** If the root is not null, then we need to account for it in our height.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=23)** The tree must be at least 1 in height.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=28)** Now this works if the height of the tree is 0 or 1, but a given root can have left and right subtrees.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=36)** In order to calculate the full height of the tree, we'll need to take these subtrees into account.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=44)** We can do that by using our function recursively.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=50)** We'll calculate the height of the left subtree by calling this same FindHeight function, but we'll pass in root.Left.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=64)** Then we'll do the same for the right.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=70)** Now we have the height of the right and left subtrees.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=75)** The total height will be this level plus the maximum of the left and right subtrees.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=85)** That's our implementation.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=90)** Let's take a look at the test code.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=92)** Here we have a root, so the height of the tree is at least 1.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=97)** Then we have left and right subtrees.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=101)** This makes the height 2.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=103)** The left subtree also has its own subtrees, left and right.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=109)** This makes the height 3.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=112)** Let's run it.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=115)** And we get what we expect in the output.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/c-sharp-algorithms/solution-find-height-of-binary-tree?u=76281980&t=119)** Thinking of time complexity, this function takes O(n) time because we need to visit every node of the tree in order to calculate the height.

> **CLI Commands:** node (1)
